  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f4a7c688-bf9f-4b1b-aa8b-5c65e75e6ce1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer8245623827644434589">Reena Hale’s destiny was shaped in the destructive—yet fascinatingly beautiful—fire that leveled her family’s pizzeria when she was young. Now an arson investigator, she finds her strength and wits constantly tested, although sometimes the job seems like a snap compared to her love life. But she can’t always blame the men.   <span id="freeText8245623827644434589" style="display:none">Reena Hale’s destiny was shaped in the destructive—yet fascinatingly beautiful—fire that leveled her family’s pizzeria when she was young. Now an arson investigator, she finds her strength and wits constantly tested, although sometimes the job seems like a snap compared to her love life. But she can’t always blame the men. After all, a soot-caked woman barking orders and smelling of smoke isn’t the biggest turn-on in the world. Then she meets Bo Goodnight, who seems different. He’s been trying to find Reena for years, and now that she’s close enough to touch, he has no intention of letting go.<br /><br />Nor does the man who has begun to haunt Reena’s life—with taunting phone calls and a string of horrifying crimes. And as Reena tries desperately to trace the origins—of the calls, the fires, the hatred aimed in her direction—she will step into the worst inferno she has ever faced...</span>
  <a data-text-id="8245623827644434589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/771865-i-enjoyed-the-book-but-i-had-a-really-hard">I enjoyed the book but I had a really hard time with one thing. She was an expert in arson and was a very smart girl..... so does anyone really think it would take her so long to figure out what was happening? I mean how could she not see who was doing all these things?</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/23109848-tammy-wight"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/23109848-tammy-wight">Tammy Wight</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">She's looking at fires all the time. The crimes all happened years apart and even though she studied the first one after graduation, learned the detai<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">She's looking at fires all the time. The crimes all happened years apart and even though she studied the first one after graduation, learned the details of Hugh's, it was not done at the same time. The explanation for Hugh's seemed very shut and done at the time. Josh - I think she had asked and finally had to believe the conclusion the investigators had made. The jerk's car was different and didn't even tie at the time.<br />That at least was my justification. You have to remember the book encompasses a twenty year period.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1666716628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1666716628" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666716628?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425278420" href="/book/show/23398641-blue-smoke">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-iin-2016">reviewed-iin-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=alternating-povs">alternating-povs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666716628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5911420548738863092">Nora’s books are one of my most reliable cures at times when my brain begs for a much needed rest. All of us readers have this amazing capacity to shut down and unplug, and for me, the best way to achieve this state of complete detachment from my everyday troubles is through one of Nora’s books. While I don’t much care for her paranormal work (PNR is just not my genre), no one writes romantic suspense better than she. <br/><br/>Blue Smoke is an old one, released more than ten years ago, but aside from the</span>
  <span id="freeText5911420548738863092" style="display:none">Nora’s books are one of my most reliable cures at times when my brain begs for a much needed rest. All of us readers have this amazing capacity to shut down and unplug, and for me, the best way to achieve this state of complete detachment from my everyday troubles is through one of Nora’s books. While I don’t much care for her paranormal work (PNR is just not my genre), no one writes romantic suspense better than she. <br><br>Blue Smoke is an old one, released more than ten years ago, but aside from the years on each chapter, nothing about it seems outdated. It begins as Nora’s story so often do, with our heroine’s childhood and the traumatic event that will determine the course of her life. From the very beginning, Catarina Hale stands out among her brothers and sisters. She is intelligent, inquisitive and systematic, a child that is never really a child. When a fire takes away her family’s livelihood, Reena knows exactly what she wants to be when she grows up. Everything from that point on is just another step toward her desired career as a fire investigator.<br><br>We follow Reena through various stages of her life, from one traumatic event to the next. While her career is on an accelerated path, her love life is miserable from the start. Somehow Reena’s love interests, no matter how superficial, always end up dead, and their death always involves fire. It takes a while for Reena to connect the dots, but not so long to make us doubt her intelligence. <br><br>As usual, Nora gives us a strong, independent heroine. She doesn’t need a man to save her, and even when the right one comes along, she doesn’t just hand over the reins. If anything, Reena is reluctant to share her life, but Bo Goodnight is just a bit too hard to resist. As we follow Reena through her education and the beginnings of her career, Bo is always in the background, dreaming about the mysterious girl he’s never had a chance to meet. Even though he’s just a touch too perfect, as Nora’s heroes tend to be, he is precisely what our Reena needs. I adored these two together and I appreciated how much time Nora took to develop a true relationship between them.<br><br>Even when her books are not perfect, I never hesitate to recommend Nora – not that she needs my recommendation. The woman is simply magical. Sinking into her story is one of my favorite feelings in the world. <br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_39714757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39714757" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1066369-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451570244p2/1066369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39714757?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1066369-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066369-jennifer?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066369-jennifer?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer39714757&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39714757" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9615877345101034149">Prior to reading a book, especially when I have several other books to read on my "to-read" shelf, I check out Amazon.com's reviews. There were quite a few positive reviews for this book but more than a fair share of people slamming the book for one reason or another. Not certain what I was getting into, I read the book with lowered expectations and was pleasantly surprised.<br/><br/>When she was eleven, Reena watched her parents' Italian restaurant burn. It was arson, the culprit went to jail, and Reena </span>
  <span id="freeText9615877345101034149" style="display:none">Prior to reading a book, especially when I have several other books to read on my "to-read" shelf, I check out Amazon.com's reviews. There were quite a few positive reviews for this book but more than a fair share of people slamming the book for one reason or another. Not certain what I was getting into, I read the book with lowered expectations and was pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />When she was eleven, Reena watched her parents' Italian restaurant burn. It was arson, the culprit went to jail, and Reena found her life's work - investigating arson fires. The novel starts when Reena was eleven and in the first couple of hundred pages follows her at various points in her life as tragedy takes the life of her boyfriend, an almost boyfriend, and another fire is set to frame her. The isolated incidents take place over the course of 10 years, so while it is obvious to the reader that Reena is being singled out, it is not obvious to her.<br /><br />At thirty-one, Reena buys a house next door to Bo Goodnight (great hero, but seriously horrible name, how high of a cheese factor can you get?). Bo has glimpsed Reena through the years at various points, once at a party, another time at the mall, once in traffic, but he has always been thwarted from actually being able to meet no matter how hard he tried to reach her. One of the highlights of the book is Reena stepping out into her back yard and meeting Bo for the first time. This is a funny, endearing scene that really had me liking Bo.<br /><br />For those who are fans of J.D. Robb, this book will be a fun and great read for you. I'm a Nora Roberts fan, and I am also the first to admit that not all of her books are winners (the Key trilogy was unreadable). "Blue Smoke" is a fun book and an entertaining read. Reena has a large family that she is close to and spends a lot of time with, people in the neighborhood know her, and reading about her life and her neighborhood was enjoyable. <br /><br />The romance is enjoyable, too, with two characters who do not treat each other horribly or get into stupid misunderstandings or fight for no reason. I particularly like to read romances where the main characters are not stupid or mean with each other, and this is a great example of that. The most believable romance stories to me are the ones where the characters like each other, respect each other, and have a fairly easy going relationship with each other. This novel illustrates the joy of that type of relationship.<br /><br />In reading the unfavorable reviews, I think that Nora Roberts is in a very difficult position. There are many people who love the familiarity in a Roberts novel, the known happily ever after, the type of hero and heroines she writes, the kind of families she showcases. I think that when she writes books with these signature elements some people really enjoy them and some people wail "She's in a rut!" <br /><br />However, when she branches out and does something different with her novels, as she does here, the reverse happens, people are upset that they had to read almost 200 pages before the main romance kicks in, while much of the book is relegated to solving a mystery that the readers have solved from page one.<br /><br />None of these factors really dulled my enjoyment of the book. I tend to like Roberts' work, especially when she does something out of the ordinary. She writes well and even the beginning parts that I knew ahead of time would contain tragedy were extremely entertaining to read because Roberts is simply an excellent writer. I enjoyed the book immensely, in part due to the big family, the friendships, and sense of community she imbues this novel with.<br /><br />I'm pleased that Nora Roberts continues to write different types of novels without paying too much attention to the criticism she receives. She can't please everyone, but her popularity shows that she does please the majority of people the majority of the time. <br /><br />If you do not like her J.D. Robb books, give this one a pass, but for those who enjoy reading Roberts for her excellent writing, you will enjoy "Blue Smoke".</span>
  <a data-text-id="9615877345101034149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11121618957610843410">DNF at page 282<br/><br/>It was: "Started off well went meh in the middle the briefly picked up again" By that time though, I didn't care anymore.<br/><br/>At first I liked Reena, even if she seemed a little unrealistic at times. While I loved Bowen Goodnight, I never felt the chemistry between them</span>
  <span id="freeText11121618957610843410" style="display:none">DNF at page 282<br /><br />It was: "Started off well went meh in the middle the briefly picked up again" By that time though, I didn't care anymore.<br /><br />At first I liked Reena, even if she seemed a little unrealistic at times. I would love to have that good of a memory sometimes. Loved her family and the pizza place, the pride everyone took in it.<br /><br />Reena started to lose her appeal... not that she got on my nerves exactly, I just stopped caring. While I loved Bowen Goodnight, I never felt the chemistry between them, even during the two love scenes I read (my eyes glazed over a couple times actually). The baseball game date was cute but *shrugs*<br /><br />We go through different periods of Reena's life, and while it was probably necessary to build her history and character up it just felt overlong. It was around page 170 I did the mental equivalent of checking my watch.<br /><br />I guessed who the 'firebug' was pretty early but it didn't sour me any against the story, but I never felt the danger from him really. He was disturbed sure but I just couldn't muster any strong feelings toward him.<br /><br />I stuck it out till the above mentioned page count but I just couldn't anymore.<br /><br />A miss this time unfortunately but oh well, on to the next read.</span>

<div id="review_981857669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/981857669" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/981857669?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer981857669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2133132542714307575">So disappointing in so many ways. The story is spread out over twenty years and takes way, way too long getting to the "present" (2005). Roberts spends lots of time in key time periods that, sure, are integral to the story, but there is just so very much piled in. I feel like what should have been vignettes were artificially inflated to make them not just chapters, but entire <em>sections</em> of the book. Which mean that the book doesn't really <em>start</em> until it's practically over.<br/><br/>The two main characters w</span>
  <span id="freeText2133132542714307575" style="display:none">So disappointing in so many ways. The story is spread out over twenty years and takes way, way too long getting to the "present" (2005). Roberts spends lots of time in key time periods that, sure, are integral to the story, but there is just so very much piled in. I feel like what should have been vignettes were artificially inflated to make them not just chapters, but entire <em>sections</em> of the book. Which mean that the book doesn't really <em>start</em> until it's practically over.<br /><br />The two main characters were good enough, and the sole reason the book maintained its three stars. Bo is simply dreamy with his manly competence and even temper. Reena is less attractive with her hint of broken and career obsession. Her family helps make up for that, though, so it evens out on the plus column.<br /><br />The central conflict, though, the main antagonist, just doesn't work. And that's far more serious. His identity isn't really a mystery (though Roberts avoids naming him for far too long) and his obsession is pretty clear as well. But he's way too competent for what he turns out to be and that makes him way, <em>way</em> too successful for the eventual plot. This affected the ending where I was left with a sense that the cost was too much and artificially inflated at that. This made the ending feel unearned in a way that makes you reevaluate the whole story. Which is where you find that it <em>really</em> doesn't work because not only was the bad guy too competent in the end, but he was more competent than he should have been all the way up front, too.<br /><br />So yeah, I felt fundamentally cheated and manipulated with the main plot and ended up wishing that this had been a straight-forward romance rather than one of Roberts' thrillers.<br /><br /><strong>A note about Steamy</strong>: Another area I felt robbed as the main characters get essentially one decent intimate scene with two half-hearted sketches later that feel peremptory, at best. This is made worse by dragging us through another scene with Reena and somebody else and I actually kind of hate that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2133132542714307575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:

<span id="freeTextContainer13163061060198093216">BLUE SMOKE (Romantic Thriller-Baltimore-Cont) – G+<br/>Roberts, Nora – Standalone<br/>Putnam, 2005- Hardcover<br/>When Reena Hale was 12 years old, events lead to her family's restaurant being burnt by an arsonist. With that, Reena was determined to become an arson investigator with the Baltimore police. Other fires have touched those know to Reena, but now it has become very personal and very dangerous.<br/>*** I am a huge fan of Ms. Roberts work and applaud her moving more into stories where the emphasis is more </span>
  <span id="freeText13163061060198093216" style="display:none">BLUE SMOKE (Romantic Thriller-Baltimore-Cont) – G+<br />Roberts, Nora – Standalone<br />Putnam, 2005- Hardcover<br />When Reena Hale was 12 years old, events lead to her family's restaurant being burnt by an arsonist. With that, Reena was determined to become an arson investigator with the Baltimore police. Other fires have touched those know to Reena, but now it has become very personal and very dangerous.<br />*** I am a huge fan of Ms. Roberts work and applaud her moving more into stories where the emphasis is more on the mystery than the romance. This was a well-crafted story, beginning when Reena is young and traveling through experiences in her life to present day. The excellent characters, relationships, dialogue and sense of place, along with the romance and intimate scenes that are the hallmark of Robert's writing are all here. The only problem I had was that you know the villain from the beginning, so it does diminish the element of suspense. Still, it is understandable that Reena doesn't put it together until the end and the final scenes bring the suspense into the story. There is graphic violence and profanity, but it's realistic and clear that Roberts did her research on fires. Roberts is an excellent writer who has a permanent place on my "must buy" list. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6491636285805923954">This was a reread for me, and I think I liked it even more the second time. Obviously the suspense was muted, but I was surprised at how many details I had forgotten about the fires and deaths. This time I was able to concentrate more on the emotions and interactions of the characters, and this was simply wonderful! I know some readers were disappointed with the slow development - Reena and Bo didn't even meet until nearly 200 pages into the story! - but to me the strength of this story is in th</span>
  <span id="freeText6491636285805923954" style="display:none">This was a reread for me, and I think I liked it even more the second time. Obviously the suspense was muted, but I was surprised at how many details I had forgotten about the fires and deaths. This time I was able to concentrate more on the emotions and interactions of the characters, and this was simply wonderful! I know some readers were disappointed with the slow development - Reena and Bo didn't even meet until nearly 200 pages into the story! - but to me the strength of this story is in the gradual buildup of events through the years, which actually puts more tension into the current-day events. Above all, I loved the strength of family love and support that Ms. Roberts shows us throughout this story, and the way the Hale family extended that love so completely and naturally to Bo.<br /><br />Here's a couple of my favorite 'mom-isms' from Mrs. Hale: <br />"We're still your parents, and we'll be your parents a hundred years after you're dead."<br />"Your father has realized what was obvious - that I was right."<br /><br />I come from a large family, so this line just seemed so natural to me: "The floor was littered with kids of varying ages, with adults stepping over or around them." <i>Yup, that's how it's done!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6491636285805923954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_21548928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21548928" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21548928?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=jens-personal-read">jens-personal-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21548928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15260244472834312213">When Catarina "Reena" Hale was eleven years old, she watched with her family--father Gib, mother Bianca, sister Francesca, sister Isabella, and brother Xander--as their family business, Sirico's, burned to the ground. The case came to a swift conclusion, when the father of a boy who had attempted to assault Reena is picked up for arson. The family rebuilds their business, their family ties stay strong, and their love and respect in the neighborhood grows. <br/><br/>We fast-forward to Reena in college, whe</span>
  <span id="freeText15260244472834312213" style="display:none">When Catarina "Reena" Hale was eleven years old, she watched with her family--father Gib, mother Bianca, sister Francesca, sister Isabella, and brother Xander--as their family business, Sirico's, burned to the ground. The case came to a swift conclusion, when the father of a boy who had attempted to assault Reena is picked up for arson. The family rebuilds their business, their family ties stay strong, and their love and respect in the neighborhood grows. <br /><br />We fast-forward to Reena in college, where she's finally decided to lose her virginity to Josh, a fellow student who yearns to be a writer. After her sister Bella's dream wedding, Reena has sex with her boyfriend, returns home, and later discovers that Josh has died during a horrific apartment fire--after supposedly falling asleep in bed with a lit cigarette. <br /><br />Again, fast-forward. Reena is still in training to become an arson investigator, her life-long dream. She's a member of the police force, has worked actual fires with her fellow firefighters, and now needs to finish her training. A firefighter she was thinking of dating dies in an apparent robbery, shot and left in his burning truck. <br /><br />Still farther into the future, Reena is a full-fledged arson investigator, and tragedy finds her once again. Only days after earning her gold shield, Luke, a boyfriend whose marriage proposal she turned down, has his Mercedes burned sky-high, and of course Reena is the main suspect. After she's cleared, she's only more determined than ever to make fire her job--to find out who sets it, and why, and to bring the perpetrators to justice. <br /><br />Then she meets Bowen "Bo" Goodnight, her new next-door-neighbor, and feelings and emotions get jumbled up with the fires that seem to dog her every step. Because someone has made her their vendetta, and will stop at nothing to make sure that his own brand of justice is served. <br /><br />I loved BLUE SMOKE! Although it took me four days to read, weighing in at 437 pages and spanning twenty years, the book is a wonderful mix of engaging family saga, taut police/arson procedural, and down and out thriller. I don't agree with the other reviewers who said this book was "horror" or that Ms. Roberts delved too deeply into the mind of the killer--most romantic suspense (and this is definitely one of those books) these days go more into the who, how, and why and less on the fluff. I commend Ms. Roberts for another winning story, one which I was sad to see end. I loved reading about the Hale family and their extended relations, and I'm sure you'll be as enthralled by them as I was. <br /><br />**I have to also say that BLUE SMOKE reads a lot like Nora Robert's alter-ego, J.D. Robb, in a lot of instances. Some of the short sentences, rapid-pace dialogue, and out-loud ruminating are reminiscent of Eve Dallas, but that only adds to the allure of BLUE SMOKE, instead of taking away from it. Kudos on another winner! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15260244472834312213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_404194204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404194204?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eve" href="/user/show/10494178-eve">Eve</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10494178-eve?shelf=2020-nora">2020-nora</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10494178-eve?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10494178-eve?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10494178-eve?shelf=sassy-heroine">sassy-heroine</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404194204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2067111203108812381"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114184.Blue_Smoke' title='Blue Smoke by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1309286007l/114184._SY75_.jpg' alt='Blue Smoke by Nora Roberts' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Romantic Suspense / Thriller / Contemporary Romance<br/><br/>The Hale family lives in a Baltimore and is the second generation to run Sirico's, an Italian pizzeria. Gibson Hale married Bianca and was quickly welcomed into the family business and the growing Italian family that lived and loved richly in the neighborhood. Their children were loved, going to school and helping in the restaurant and learning the business. However, the attempted rape of 11-year-old Caterina "Reena" Hale sets into motion a </span>
  <span id="freeText2067111203108812381" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114184.Blue_Smoke" title="Blue Smoke by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1309286007l/114184._SY75_.jpg" alt="Blue Smoke by Nora Roberts" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Romantic Suspense / Thriller / Contemporary Romance<br><br>The Hale family lives in a Baltimore and is the second generation to run Sirico's, an Italian pizzeria. Gibson Hale married Bianca and was quickly welcomed into the family business and the growing Italian family that lived and loved richly in the neighborhood. Their children were loved, going to school and helping in the restaurant and learning the business. However, the attempted rape of 11-year-old Caterina "Reena" Hale sets into motion a series of events that will span 20 years, leaving death and wreckage in its wake.<br><br>Twenty years later, the heroine Reena Hale is an arson investigator and it looks like someone is seeking revenge and setting fires. That someone has done a few things in Reena's life to make her miserable, but now this all is starting to escalate out of control. The hero, Bo Goodnight, fell in love with Reena when he first saw her at a party during her college days. He can't believe his eyes when his "Dream Girl" moves in next door. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I think there's a reason you moved in next door. I think there's a reason I saw you all those years ago, but didn't meet you until now. I don't think I was ready for you until now.”</b>
</i> <br><br>This is one of my favorite stories by Nora Roberts. I really enjoyed the strong sense of family this story had (Reena's relationship with her parents and siblings was well done). Loved the romance and chemistry between Reena and Bo. There were also many sad moments, like in everyone's life. I also enjoyed that balance between suspense, thrill and romance was very well done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2067111203108812381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1017866343562461039" style="display:none">I enjoyed this to a certain point, especially young Reena but I found it much too long with lots of unnecessary filler before we get to the main story and I found the bad guy too clever (given he is setting fires and killing people for a 10 yr period and he eludes capture wreaking a ridiculous amount of havoc even after they know who he is but there is no mention of a particularly high IQ at any point) and the amount of damage he was able to inflict before they caught him ridiculously high.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6485480-blue-smoke">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7393825-malu?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7393825-malu?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7393825-malu?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3067842966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7497493427448179727">There wasn't much tension or mystery in this story. The antagonist wasn't named until more than halfway through the book but it was incredibly obvious who he was after pretty much the first chapter. I couldn't tell if Roberts wanted the reader to know who he was or if she expected it to be a surprise when he was revealed. <br/>Same thing for the romantic storyline. It was set up kind of like the main characters were meant for each other from the beginning, so as a reader I never wondered how or when </span>
  <span id="freeText7497493427448179727" style="display:none">There wasn't much tension or mystery in this story. The antagonist wasn't named until more than halfway through the book but it was incredibly obvious who he was after pretty much the first chapter. I couldn't tell if Roberts wanted the reader to know who he was or if she expected it to be a surprise when he was revealed. <br />Same thing for the romantic storyline. It was set up kind of like the main characters were meant for each other from the beginning, so as a reader I never wondered how or when they were going to get together. Because of that, even though the writing was fine there wasn't much motivation for me to keep turning the pages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7497493427448179727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText16229010298805939929" style="display:none">I loved all the intrinsic events taking place and the family bond the Hale family has. I loved the mystery and drama in this book. I literally stayed up all night reading this one.<br /><br />In 1985 Baltimore Catarina "Renna" Hale was attacked by her neighbor twelve year old Joey Pastorelli and would have been raped if the neighbors didn't intervene. Reena's father fought with Joey's abusive dad and that night, the Hale's family pizzeria, Sirico's burns to the ground. Police find enough evidence to arrest Joey's father and Joey is taken away from his mother after he burns his dog and leaves it on Reena's doorstop.<br /><br />Reena decides that she will because an arson investigator, studying hard in school to make her dream a reality. When Rena buys a house in her old neighborhood, her next door neighbor is Bo Goodnight who saw Reena at a college party years ago and fell in lust. Over the years he sighted his Dream Girl but they never met but when the pair finally get together, lust turns into something more for Bo and the commitment phobic Reena who is afraid that he might be her one and only true love. They conduct their courtship during an arson investigation in which someone is targeting Reena and the people closest to her. Reena is in a race against time to catch the killer before the body count mounts.<br /><br />Once again Nora Roberts has written a wonderful romantic thriller that is sure to hit the New York Times bestseller list. Her characterization are fantastic, the firefighting scenes are full of action and suspense and the plot moves along at a fast pace. Bo's Dream Girl is better than his fantasy of her and he is determined to woo her no matter how many obstacles she put in his path. Their love scenes are sweet, poignant sometimes downright funny. BLUE SMOKE is an example of why Ms. Roberts is one of the most popular authors writing today.<br />by<br />Harriet Klausner<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1984173995" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984173995" />
    <a title="Stephanie Kline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6801337-stephanie-kline"><img alt="Stephanie Kline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506108627p2/6801337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984173995?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Kline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Kline" href="/user/show/6801337-stephanie-kline">Stephanie Kline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984173995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9362532373856924918">I really enjoyed "Blue Smoke", and would have absolutely given it a 5-star review if it hadn't been for one thing -- this was, without a doubt, the most disturbing and twisted novel I've read of Nora Roberts'. That's not necessarily a bad thing... she does thriller/mystery stories REALLY well. But of all her stand-alone romance/suspense novels, this one dove into the mindset of the villain in WAY more graphic detail than I've read before. And there's just something about a psychopath obsessed wi</span>
  <span id="freeText9362532373856924918" style="display:none">I really enjoyed "Blue Smoke", and would have absolutely given it a 5-star review if it hadn't been for one thing -- this was, without a doubt, the most disturbing and twisted novel I've read of Nora Roberts'. That's not necessarily a bad thing... she does thriller/mystery stories REALLY well. But of all her stand-alone romance/suspense novels, this one dove into the mindset of the villain in WAY more graphic detail than I've read before. And there's just something about a psychopath obsessed with fire (and setting people on fire) that makes for uncomfortable reading (or listening via Audible, as I did). <br /><br />This novel follows Reena Hale, the youngest daughter of an adorably-close Italian family. The descriptions of the family dynamic are some of Nora's best, and the Hales are right up there with some of her best characters. When this story opens, Reena is a young girl, watching her family's Italian restaurant go up in flames. From that point on, fire becomes one of her greatest interests, and she is determined to become an arson investigator with the Baltimore police force. <br /><br />"Blue Smoke" follows Reena over a 20-year time span, through college and her young adult years, as she's training with the Baltimore police. It covers her earlier relationships before we get to the meat of the story -- a complaint that some people have had about this book. While some say that it takes too long for the "real story" to begin, I think that all the development is absolutely necessary to structure the conflict, and it makes Reena that much more authentic. The story takes on a more convincing (and therefore scarier) edge, because we see the way the danger unfolds over several years. <br /><br />Once Reena is thirty-one, the "real" story starts. She meets Bo Goodnight - a carpenter who's been in love with her since he saw her at a college party from across the room years ago. This part was a little far-fetched for me, but overall the romance was cute. Bo's a good guy, and Reena is a strong character that meshes well with him. I do, however, like the way that the suspense aspect of this novel is the star of the show - not the romance. <br /><br />But that brings me back to my only grievance. While the writing is terrific, and the book flows extremely well with action-packed scenes... it's disturbing. We're in the villain's head a LOT, which means we're getting first-hand looks at what he thinks about setting fires, watching/hearing/smelling people burn, and we're seeing him commit these terrible acts of arson, rape, and murder in excruciating detail. Nora always impresses me with her ability to get into the minds of the deranged, but it definitely made for some uncomfortable scenes (especially towards the end, when the story ramps up to its fiery (haha) conclusion). This is the ONLY reason I brought it down a star. It felt more like her darker J.D. Robb novels at times, and the "feel-good" story that I usually find with Nora's books wasn't necessarily there with this one. It left me dwelling on some pretty graphic scenes after I finished reading. <br /><br />I'd absolutely recommend this novel to any fan of Nora's, or any fan of thriller/suspense and romance in general. It's edgier and darker than most of her others, but in a fascinating way. Fully fleshed out and beautifully written, it's not to be missed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9362532373856924918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mojca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1359426-mojca"><img alt="Mojca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379576265p2/1359426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155520291?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155520291" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10549545293004109394">The rating probably reflects me having read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11422762.Chasing_Fire' title='Chasing Fire by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chasing Fire</a> just before tackling this one. And let me tell you, the books, at least for me, are worlds apart.<br/><br/><u>First problem:</u> the first half of the story. Completely redundant, IMO, I couldn’t care less for Reena’s life story spanning twenty years from the beginning of the novel until the story actually began. I couldn’t care less for her choices of boyfriends until the right man came along...<br/><u>Second problem:</u> the heroine. I simply couldn’t bring myself t</span>
  <span id="freeText10549545293004109394" style="display:none">The rating probably reflects me having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11422762.Chasing_Fire" title="Chasing Fire by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Chasing Fire</a> just before tackling this one. And let me tell you, the books, at least for me, are worlds apart.<br /><br /><u>First problem:</u> the first half of the story. Completely redundant, IMO, I couldn’t care less for Reena’s life story spanning twenty years from the beginning of the novel until the story actually began. I couldn’t care less for her choices of boyfriends until the right man came along...<br /><u>Second problem:</u> the heroine. I simply couldn’t bring myself to like her. She was emotionally stumped, with no apparent reason why (I don’t deem the death of her first boyfriend reason enough, since no undying love-and-devotion confessions were exchanged). She had the worst taste in men, I didn’t like her approach to relationships, and she constantly jumped to (wrong) conclusions when the right man came along.<br /><u>Third problem:</u> the predictability. The villain was not a surprise, the whole thing wasn’t even suspenseful, so easy it was to spot. For someone as smart as she thought she was, the only surprise came from the heroine and her inability to figure it all out sooner.<br /><br />The only redeeming quality for me was the hero—Bowen “Bo” Goodnight. He was hot, sexy, romantic, silly, endearing, protective, stubborn etc. And it was a pity he was wasted on this book. And there was too little of him, even when he started being the hero, to turn the “rating tide”.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10549545293004109394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261566093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6602825311457764310">As always, it did what it was supposed to do--entertain me. If you're looking for a book that exposes deep truths about the human condition, or examines some stark reality of life, you're not going to pick up a romance. Romance reading is like watching a sitcom. It's something to take your mind on a quick trip through fantasyland for a short period of time. You're not really looking for deep analysis of symbolism, character development, or theme when you pick up a romance. But if you're going to</span>
  <span id="freeText6602825311457764310" style="display:none">As always, it did what it was supposed to do--entertain me. If you're looking for a book that exposes deep truths about the human condition, or examines some stark reality of life, you're not going to pick up a romance. Romance reading is like watching a sitcom. It's something to take your mind on a quick trip through fantasyland for a short period of time. You're not really looking for deep analysis of symbolism, character development, or theme when you pick up a romance. But if you're going to read a mindless romance, Nora Roberts is the way to go. Her prose is fluent, her characters likable, and she totally nails dialogue--it's her gift. So if you're looking for a read you can whiz through and just enjoy the story, then she's your girl!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14333021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer450386561914917115">I really enjoyed this. I liked how Reena and Bo circled around each other for years. It did seem that it took Reena a bit too long to connect all the fires together. I mean, who has fire touch their life *that* much? And the ending seemed a little rushed. But all in all, it was romantic and suspenseful, as any good Nora Roberts should be.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2708071939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2708071939" />
    <a title="Geniee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87076326-geniee"><img alt="Geniee" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2708071939?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geniee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geniee" href="/user/show/87076326-geniee">Geniee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87076326-geniee?shelf=firefighter">firefighter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2708071939&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2708071939" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7661510841671485684">Nora has brought us another strong willed character, stubborn even.<br/>But she builds her backstory actually very well to present us with the reasons as to why she is how she is, instead of just telling us.<br/>The anthagonist is somewhat skilled and cunning, and plays his part in the story as good as he can, because he is ultimately weak minded and his motives to do his deeds are weak at best, deeply misguided and, honestly, off schedule.<br/>His predatory, no, his stalkery behaviour is pathetic at best. He </span>
  <span id="freeText7661510841671485684" style="display:none">Nora has brought us another strong willed character, stubborn even.<br />But she builds her backstory actually very well to present us with the reasons as to why she is how she is, instead of just telling us.<br />The anthagonist is somewhat skilled and cunning, and plays his part in the story as good as he can, because he is ultimately weak minded and his motives to do his deeds are weak at best, deeply misguided and, honestly, off schedule.<br />His predatory, no, his stalkery behaviour is pathetic at best. He waits years between strikes and is inconsistent in his motives, in who he strikes and when.<br />But I consider this an actually relaxing-ish read, because the heroine's family dinamycs (althought not as deeply explored as one would like) are adorable and warm, with a cozy, Italian? vibe. She beneficts from a vast family with steady support, and joyfull and playfull cousins and brothers.<br />As for the love interest... It could have better introduced.<br />He comes off as a little much at the first REAL, face to face, meeting, and then just cools the jets FAST. Not consistent with his WOW YOU ARE THAT GIRL OF MY LIFE OMG YOU ARE REAL. And then we get waaaay less of that side of him.<br />The first time he sees her, love at first sight, yes. Second time, years later sees her again, runs after her car, fate. Third time he sees her? Could have maybe have remain a little calm, and not just invaded her private property, as we all know that that kind of thing is creepy and a woman living alone, gun or not would have gone running for the hills. Since it was established she actually moved next door, she wasn't just going to vanish, and he would've had time to make a less confusing, borderline outlandish, first impression.<br />The vilain "blindfold" - as I like to call the twist where the decoy villain, who then turns out, in a big reveal, that he actually wasn't the bad guy all along! - could have bewn better orchestraded.<br />But still, in the end it was still a good read. Won't get your cortisol levels up there. Calming to the soul, good with a good chlichê "Rose water bath with some Chardonnay and some cinnamon scented candles".</span>
  <a data-text-id="7661510841671485684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qTEf/JkxWO2RLAtg9KTlRXVob9BUGhZf5vKGou22suRR+ZU8SXiz1Hr/NWkIYApkveTDq9Tndd1/FV3T5i4atA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts">About Nora Roberts</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1505847251p3/625.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14475473949675602391">Nora Roberts is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of more than 200 novels, including Hideaway, Under Currents, Come Sundown and coming in November 2020 -- The Awakening -- the first book in The Dragon Heart Legacy. She is also the author of the futuristic suspense In Death series written under the pen name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb' title='J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.D. Robb</a>. There are more than 500 million copies of her books in print.</span>
